The 3-second-between-requests rule was always documented, but enforcement got strict starting in late 2024 / early 2025.\"}},{\"@type\":\"Question\",\"name\":\"Is Semantic Scholar's 1,000 req/sec really shared?\",\"acceptedAnswer\":{\"@type\":\"Answer\",\"text\":\"Yes — that's the unauthenticated pool, shared across every IP that hits the public API. In practice, unauthenticated requests start failing during peak hours regardless of your individual rate. The official advice is to apply for an API key, which moves you to a per-key bucket. Application takes weeks and is granted on the assumption of academic, not commercial, use.\"}},{\"@type\":\"Question\",\"name\":\"What about PubMed's E-utils?\",\"acceptedAnswer\":{\"@type\":\"Answer\",\"text\":\"Better than the others — 3 req/sec without a key, 10 req/sec with. Apply for an NCBI API key by email; usually granted same-day for stated research purposes. Still: 10 req/sec is fine for a single user but inadequate for a multi-user product where every user-question fans out to several PubMed calls.\"}},{\"@type\":\"Question\",\"name\":\"Why does PaperQA2 work where my homegrown agent doesn't?\",\"acceptedAnswer\":{\"@type\":\"Answer\",\"text\":\"Three reasons. (1) PaperQA2 batches and caches aggressively — the same DOI lookup is never made twice. (2) It uses Semantic Scholar primarily for its citation graph (one call per paper) rather than as a search index. (3) It accepts a longer wall-clock per question in exchange for not exceeding limits. If you want the same UX in a product where users expect 5-second responses, you need a higher-throughput layer.\"}},{\"@type\":\"Question\",\"name\":\"What does API Pick Academic Search actually solve?\",\"acceptedAnswer\":{\"@type\":\"Answer\",\"text\":\"It manages the rate limits and source coverage so your agent doesn't have to. One POST /api/search/academic call returns ranked results from arXiv, PubMed, bioRxiv, and medRxiv together, pre-shaped for LLM consumption. 5 credits per call (≈$0.005), only deducted on HTTP 200. You get to focus on the agent loop and the prompt; the throttling is our problem.\"}}]}</script><script type=\"application/ld+json\">{\"@context\":\"https://schema.org\",\"@type\":\"HowTo\",\"name\":\"How to Build a Scientific Literature-Review Agent Without Getting Rate-Limited\",\"description\":\"arXiv 429s, Semantic Scholar's shared rate limit, PubMed's 3-per-second cap — the rate limits on free academic APIs are eating LLM-driven research agents. sm:px-6 py-12\"><header class=\"mb-10\"><div class=\"flex items-center gap-3 mb-5\"><span class=\"spec-tag\">[ blog · <!-- -->tutorial<!-- --> ]</span><span class=\"h-px flex-1 max-w-[80px] bg-gradient-to-r from-zinc-300 to-transparent dark:from-zinc-700\"></span><span class=\"spec-tag !text-cyan-700 dark:!text-cyan-400\">10<!-- --> min read</span></div><h1 class=\"text-3xl md:text-[42px] font-bold tracking-tight text-zinc-900 dark:text-white mb-4 leading-[1.1]\">How to Build a Scientific Literature-Review Agent Without Getting Rate-Limited</h1><div class=\"flex flex-wrap items-center gap-x-3 gap-y-1 text-sm text-gray-600 dark:text-gray-400\"><span class=\"font-medium text-gray-800 dark:text-gray-200\">Sarah Choy</span><span aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"text-gray-300 dark:text-zinc-700\">·</span><span>Published May 3, 2026</span><span aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"text-gray-300 dark:text-zinc-700\">·</span><span>10 min read</span></div><div class=\"mt-6 mb-8 rounded-md overflow-hidden border border-zinc-200 dark:border-zinc-800 relative\"><span class=\"absolute -top-1.5 -left-1.5 h-3 w-3 border-t border-l border-zinc-400/60 dark:border-cyan-500/40 z-10\"></span><span class=\"absolute -top-1.5 -right-1.5 h-3 w-3 border-t border-r border-zinc-400/60 dark:border-cyan-500/40 z-10\"></span><span class=\"absolute -bottom-1.5 -left-1.5 h-3 w-3 border-b border-l border-zinc-400/60 dark:border-cyan-500/40 z-10\"></span><span class=\"absolute -bottom-1.5 -right-1.5 h-3 w-3 border-b border-r border-zinc-400/60 dark:border-cyan-500/40 z-10\"></span><img src=\"/og/blog/scientific-literature-agent-without-rate-limits.webp\" alt=\"How to Build a Scientific Literature-Review Agent Without Getting Rate-Limited\" class=\"w-full h-auto block\"></div><p class=\"text-lg text-zinc-600 dark:text-zinc-300 leading-relaxed\">Build a literature-review agent on raw arXiv + PubMed + Semantic Scholar today and you'll hit 429s before you finish ten papers. Here's why the rate limits got worse, what PaperQA / Undermind actually do under the hood, and a working pattern that survives a real review session.</p><section aria-label=\"TL;DR\" class=\"my-6 rounded-lg border border-brand-200 dark:border-brand-900/60 bg-brand-50/60 dark:bg-brand-950/20 p-5\"><h2 class=\"text-sm font-bold tracking-widest uppercase text-brand-700 dark:text-brand-400 mb-3\">TL;DR</h2><ul class=\"space-y-2 text-gray-800 dark:text-gray-200 text-base leading-7\"><li class=\"flex gap-2\"><span class=\"text-brand-600 dark:text-brand-500 select-none\">•</span><span>arXiv began throttling aggressively in late 2024 after LLM scrapers triggered 429 storms; the documented limit is 1 request every 3 seconds, but real-world burst tolerance is lower.</span></li><li class=\"flex gap-2\"><span class=\"text-brand-600 dark:text-brand-500 select-none\">•</span><span>Semantic Scholar's 1,000 req/sec is shared across all unauthenticated callers — effectively unusable for production agents.</span></li><li class=\"flex gap-2\"><span class=\"text-brand-600 dark:text-brand-500 select-none\">•</span><span>PubMed E-utils caps unauthenticated traffic at 3 req/sec; with an API key, 10 req/sec.</span></li><li class=\"flex gap-2\"><span class=\"text-brand-600 dark:text-brand-500 select-none\">•</span><span>Working agents (PaperQA2, Undermind, Elicit) all use a proxy / cache layer in front of these sources.</span></li><li class=\"flex gap-2\"><span class=\"text-brand-600 dark:text-brand-500 select-none\">•</span><span>API Pick Academic Search wraps arXiv, PubMed, bioRxiv, and medRxiv in one rate-managed endpoint — 5 credits per call, only-on-success.</span></li></ul></section></header><h2 id=\"the-problem-in-one-paragraph\" class=\"scroll-mt-24 text-2xl md:text-3xl font-bold tracking-tight text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-12 mb-4\">The problem in one paragraph</h2><p class=\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\">Free academic APIs are wonderful and they're being eaten alive. arXiv, PubMed, and Semantic Scholar were designed in an era when 'one researcher writes a script that polls every few seconds' was the worst-case load. Now every undergraduate with Python writes an LLM agent that fans out fifty parallel calls to read one paper's references. Multiply by thousands of similar agents and you get the pattern arXiv staff describe on X as the \"arXiv-pocalypse\" of late 2024 — sustained Rate Exceeded responses, degraded service, and a wave of new throttling rules that hit indie builders harder than the bad actors.</p><p class=\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\">The result: a literature-review agent that works on five papers in dev environment falls over halfway through a real review session. The user gets a half-finished answer with three citations instead of fifteen.</p><p class=\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\">This article is about how to build the agent so that doesn't happen.</p><h2 id=\"whats-actually-rate-limited-and-where\" class=\"scroll-mt-24 text-2xl md:text-3xl font-bold tracking-tight text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-12 mb-4\">What's actually rate-limited and where</h2><div class=\"my-6 overflow-x-auto rounded-lg border border-gray-200 dark:border-zinc-800\"><div class=\"px-4 py-2 text-xs text-gray-500 dark:text-gray-400 border-b border-gray-200 dark:border-zinc-800 bg-gray-50 dark:bg-zinc-900/60\">Rate limits documented at the time of writing. arXiv and Semantic Scholar both reserve the right to throttle harder during incidents — verify before high-volume integration.</div><table class=\"w-full text-sm\"><thead><tr class=\"bg-gray-50 dark:bg-zinc-900/60 text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-200\"><th class=\"text-start font-semibold px-4 py-3 bg-brand-50 dark:bg-brand-950/40 text-brand-700 dark:text-brand-400\">API Pick Academic</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr class=\"border-b border-gray-100 dark:border-zinc-800/70 last:border-0\"><th preprints</td><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300\">Biomedical (35M+ records)</td><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300\">Cross-disciplinary dark:text-gray-300\">100k req / day</td><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 bg-brand-50/40 dark:bg-brand-950/20\">Pay-per-call, no per-user throttle</td></tr><tr class=\"border-b border-gray-100 dark:border-zinc-800/70 last:border-0\"><th class=\"text-start font-medium px-4 py-3 text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 align-top\">Rate limit (with key)</th><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300\">Same — keys for bulk only</td><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300\">10 req / sec</td><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300\">Per-key bucket (granted slowly)</td><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300\">Same</td><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 bg-brand-50/40 dark:bg-brand-950/20\">—</td></tr><tr class=\"border-b border-gray-100 dark:border-zinc-800/70 last:border-0\"><th class=\"text-start font-medium px-4 py-3 text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 align-top\">Returns full text?</th><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300\">Yes (XML / PDF link)</td><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300\">Abstract only</td><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300\">Abstract + selected paywall-free</td><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300\">Abstract + selected</td><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 bg-brand-50/40 dark:bg-brand-950/20\">Title + URL + abstract-shaped snippet</td></tr><tr class=\"border-b border-gray-100 dark:border-zinc-800/70 last:border-0\"><th class=\"text-start font-medium px-4 py-3 text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 align-top\">LLM-friendly format</th><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300\">No — Atom XML</td><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300\">No — XML</td><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300\">Yes — JSON</td><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300\">Yes — JSON</td><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 bg-brand-50/40 dark:bg-brand-950/20\">Yes — JSON, snippets pre-shaped</td></tr><tr class=\"border-b border-gray-100 dark:border-zinc-800/70 last:border-0\"><th class=\"text-start font-medium px-4 py-3 text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 align-top\">Cost</th><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300\">Free</td><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300\">Free (key recommended)</td><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300\">Free, key required for production</td><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300\">Free</td><td class=\"px-4 py-3 align-top text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 bg-brand-50/40 dark:bg-brand-950/20\">5 credits/call (~$0.005)</td></tr></tbody></table></div><h2 id=\"what-working-products-actually-do\" class=\"scroll-mt-24 text-2xl md:text-3xl font-bold tracking-tight text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-12 mb-4\">What working products actually do</h2><p class=\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\">PaperQA2, Undermind, Elicit, ResearchRabbit, and the agentic RAG papers (e.g. <em>Open-Source Agentic Hybrid RAG Framework</em>, arXiv 2508.05660) all converge on a similar pattern. Three engineering moves matter most:</p><h3 id=\"1-cache-by-doi-arxiv-id-not-by-query\" class=\"scroll-mt-24 text-xl font-semibold text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-8 mb-3\">1. Cache by DOI / arXiv ID, not by query</h3><p class=\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\">The same paper gets requested by many different queries. Caching at the search-result level barely helps; caching at the paper-identifier level does. A small Redis (or even SQLite) layer keyed on <code class=\"font-mono text-[0.85em] bg-gray-100 dark:bg-zinc-800 text-brand-700 dark:text-brand-400 px-1.5 py-0.5 rounded\">doi:10.1038/...</code> pays itself back in one afternoon of agent traffic.</p><h3 id=\"2-treat-the-citation-graph-as-the-slow-changing-index\" class=\"scroll-mt-24 text-xl font-semibold text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-8 mb-3\">2. Treat the citation graph as the slow-changing index</h3><p class=\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\">Semantic Scholar's strength isn't keyword search; it's the citation graph. PaperQA2 uses it to expand from one seed paper to a related cluster, not to discover papers from scratch. That's a much smaller request volume — one call per paper, not hundreds — and stays well under the rate limit.</p><h3 id=\"3-accept-latency-as-the-trade-off-or-proxy-the-rate-limit\" class=\"scroll-mt-24 text-xl font-semibold text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-8 mb-3\">3. Accept latency as the trade-off, OR proxy the rate limit</h3><p class=\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\">Either you make users wait 30-60 seconds for a careful, throttle-respecting query (PaperQA2's choice), or you add a layer that aggregates traffic across users and presents a single burst-tolerant interface to the agent (the API Pick choice). Both work. Mixing them — a low-latency UX over rate-limited public APIs without a buffer — is what fails.</p><h2 id=\"working-code-a-literature-agent-that-finishes\" class=\"scroll-mt-24 text-2xl md:text-3xl font-bold tracking-tight text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-12 mb-4\">Working code: a literature agent that finishes</h2><p class=\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\">The minimum viable agent </span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(301, 63%, 40%)\">return</span><span> </span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(119, 34%, 47%)\">\"\\n\"</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">.</span><span>join</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">(</span><span>b</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">.</span><span>text </span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(301, 63%, 40%)\">for</span><span> b </span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(301, 63%, 40%)\">in</span><span> r</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">.</span><span>content </span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(301, 63%, 40%)\">if</span><span> b</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">.</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(119, 34%, 47%)\">type</span><span> </span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(221, 87%, 60%)\">==</span><span> </span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(119, 34%, 47%)\">\"text\"</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">)</span><span>\n</span></span><span><span>        </span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(301, 63%, 40%)\">if</span><span> r</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">.</span><span>stop_reason </span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(221, 87%, 60%)\">==</span><span> </span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(119, 34%, 47%)\">\"tool_use\"</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">:</span><span>\n</span></span><span><span>            results </span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(221, 87%, 60%)\">=</span><span> </span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">[</span><span>call_tool</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">(</span><span>b</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">)</span><span> </span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(301, 63%, 40%)\">for</span><span> b </span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(301, 63%, 40%)\">in</span><span> r</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">.</span><span>content </span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(301, 63%, 40%)\">if</span><span> b</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">.</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(119, 34%, 47%)\">type</span><span> </span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(221, 87%, 60%)\">==</span><span> </span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(119, 34%, 47%)\">\"tool_use\"</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">]</span><span>\n</span></span><span><span>            msgs</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">.</span><span>append</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">(</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">{</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(119, 34%, 47%)\">\"role\"</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">:</span><span> </span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(119, 34%, 47%)\">\"user\"</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">,</span><span> </span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(119, 34%, 47%)\">\"content\"</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">:</span><span> results</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">}</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">)</span><span>\n</span></span><span>\n</span><span><span></span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(301, 63%, 40%)\">print</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">(</span><span>review</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">(</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(119, 34%, 47%)\">\"Recent advances in LLM-based protein structure prediction (2025)\"</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">)</span><span class=\"token\" style=\"color:hsl(230, 8%, 24%)\">)</span></span></code></pre></div></div><p class=\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\">Cost per question:</p><ul class=\"list-disc ms-6 space-y-2 text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\"><li>1-2 academic_search calls (5-10 credits = $0.005-$0.010)</li><li>1 extract call covering 3-5 papers (6-10 credits = $0.006-$0.010)</li><li>~5,000 input + 1,200 output tokens to Claude (~$0.04)</li></ul><p class=\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\">Round figure: ~5 cents per literature-review answer with citations. At 100 questions/day that's $5/day — about what one reasonable researcher's daily caffeine costs.</p><aside class=\"my-6 rounded-lg border px-4 py-3 text-sm leading-6 bg-violet-50 dark:bg-violet-950/40 border-violet-200 dark:border-violet-900 text-violet-900 dark:text-violet-100\"><div class=\"font-semibold mb-1\">When NOT to use this pattern</div><div>Bulk literature mining (downloading millions of papers for training data) is a different problem. Use OpenAlex bulk dumps for that — they're explicitly designed for it and free. The pattern in this article is for interactive, per-question agent calls where users wait for answers in seconds, not hours.</div></aside><h2 id=\"sub-vertical-tweaks\" class=\"scroll-mt-24 text-2xl md:text-3xl font-bold tracking-tight text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-12 mb-4\">Sub-vertical tweaks</h2><h3 id=\"biomedical-literature\" class=\"scroll-mt-24 text-xl font-semibold text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-8 mb-3\">Biomedical literature</h3><p class=\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\">Bias the agent toward PubMed (peer-reviewed) and explicitly mark bioRxiv/medRxiv hits as preprints. When asking <em>\"what does the latest evidence say\"</em>, the agent should weight peer-reviewed higher. A line in the system prompt — <em>\"If preprint and peer-reviewed sources disagree, defer to peer-reviewed and note the discrepancy\"</em> — handles this cleanly.</p><h3 id=\"mathematical-cs\" class=\"scroll-mt-24 text-xl font-semibold text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-8 mb-3\">Mathematical / CS</h3><p class=\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\">arXiv dominates here. The signal-to-noise ratio is better than in biomed, and citations matter more than recency for foundational work. Search with broader queries and let the agent prune.</p><h3 id=\"drug-discovery-clinical\" class=\"scroll-mt-24 text-xl font-semibold text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-8 mb-3\">Drug discovery / clinical</h3><p class=\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\">Pair with <a class=\"text-brand-700 dark:text-brand-400 hover:underline underline-offset-2\" href=\"/search-clinical\">Clinical Search</a> (ClinicalTrials.gov + FDA labels + ChEMBL + DrugBank) for the regulatory and bioactivity dimensions that academic search can't cover. The combination — peer-reviewed literature + trial registry + structural data — is how a drug-repurposing or pharmacovigilance agent gets useful.</p><h2 id=\"where-this-generalises\" class=\"scroll-mt-24 text-2xl md:text-3xl font-bold tracking-tight text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-12 mb-4\">Where this generalises</h2><p class=\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\">The rate-limit problem is not unique to academic search. Any open public dataset that shipped APIs in the pre-LLM era is being subjected to the same load patterns now: SEC EDGAR, USPTO, EPO, public-records databases, weather services, government open data. The same engineering pattern works for all of them — cache at the entity level, layer a managed proxy, accept latency as the alternative when you can't afford the proxy.</p><p class=\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\">The deeper shift: in 2026 it's no longer reasonable to expect a free public API to absorb LLM-agent load directly. The endpoints aren't disappearing — but they're getting wrapped by a layer of paid managed services that exists to translate \"polite human researcher\" rate limits into \"burst-tolerant agent traffic\". <a class=\"text-brand-700 dark:text-brand-400 hover:underline underline-offset-2\" href=\"/search-academic\">API Pick Academic Search</a> is one of those layers for the literature-review use case. Expect more.</p><section class=\"my-12\"><h2 class=\"text-2xl font-bold text-gray-900 dark:text-white mb-6\">Frequently Asked Questions</h2><div class=\"space-y-5\"><div class=\"border-b border-gray-200 dark:border-zinc-800 pb-5\"><h3 class=\"font-semibold text-gray-900 dark:text-white mb-2 text-base\">Why did arXiv start rate-limiting so aggressively in 2024?</h3><p class=\"text-sm text-gray-600 dark:text-gray-400 leading-relaxed\">LLM-driven scrapers. arXiv staff have been explicit on their developer mailing list and on @arxiv on X about the pattern: an LLM agent fans out 50 parallel requests to fetch references for a single paper, multiply by thousands of users running similar workflows, and the whole index gets degraded. The 3-second-between-requests rule was always documented, but enforcement got strict starting in late 2024 / early 2025.</p></div><div class=\"border-b border-gray-200 dark:border-zinc-800 pb-5\"><h3 class=\"font-semibold text-gray-900 dark:text-white mb-2 text-base\">Is Semantic Scholar's 1,000 req/sec really shared?</h3><p class=\"text-sm text-gray-600 dark:text-gray-400 leading-relaxed\">Yes — that's the unauthenticated pool, shared across every IP that hits the public API. In practice, unauthenticated requests start failing during peak hours regardless of your individual rate. The official advice is to apply for an API key, which moves you to a per-key bucket. Application takes weeks and is granted on the assumption of academic, not commercial, use.</p></div><div class=\"border-b border-gray-200 dark:border-zinc-800 pb-5\"><h3 class=\"font-semibold text-gray-900 dark:text-white mb-2 text-base\">What about PubMed's E-utils?</h3><p class=\"text-sm text-gray-600 dark:text-gray-400 leading-relaxed\">Better than the others — 3 req/sec without a key, 10 req/sec with. Apply for an NCBI API key by email; usually granted same-day for stated research purposes. Still: 10 req/sec is fine for a single user but inadequate for a multi-user product where every user-question fans out to several PubMed calls.</p></div><div class=\"border-b border-gray-200 dark:border-zinc-800 pb-5\"><h3 class=\"font-semibold text-gray-900 dark:text-white mb-2 text-base\">Why does PaperQA2 work where my homegrown agent doesn't?</h3><p class=\"text-sm text-gray-600 dark:text-gray-400 leading-relaxed\">Three reasons. (1) PaperQA2 batches and caches aggressively — the same DOI lookup is never made twice. (2) It uses Semantic Scholar primarily for its citation graph (one call per paper) rather than as a search index. (3) It accepts a longer wall-clock per question in exchange for not exceeding limits. If you want the same UX in a product where users expect 5-second responses, you need a higher-throughput layer.</p></div><div class=\"border-b border-gray-200 dark:border-zinc-800 pb-5\"><h3 class=\"font-semibold text-gray-900 dark:text-white mb-2 text-base\">What does API Pick Academic Search actually solve?</h3><p class=\"text-sm text-gray-600 dark:text-gray-400 leading-relaxed\">It manages the rate limits and source coverage so your agent doesn't have to. One <code>POST /api/search/academic</code> call returns ranked results from arXiv, PubMed, bioRxiv, and medRxiv together, pre-shaped for LLM consumption. 5 credits per call (≈$0.005), only deducted on HTTP 200. You get to focus on the agent loop and the prompt; the throttling is our problem.</p></div></div></section><section class=\"my-12\"><h2 class=\"text-xl font-bold text-gray-900 dark:text-white mb-4\">APIs used in this article</h2><div class=\"grid grid-cols-1 sm:grid-cols-2 gap-3\"><a class=\"group block rounded-lg border border-gray-200 dark:border-zinc-800 bg-white dark:bg-zinc-950 p-4 hover:border-brand-300 dark:hover:border-brand-700 transition-colors\" href=\"/search-academic\"><div class=\"flex items-start gap-3\"><div class=\"shrink-0 mt-0.5\"><svg class=\"w-7 h-7 text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300\" fill=\"none\" stroke=\"currentColor\" viewBox=\"0 0 24 24\"><path stroke-linecap=\"round\" stroke-linejoin=\"round\" stroke-width=\"1.5\" d=\"M12 14l9-5-9-5-9 5 9 5zm0 0v6m-7-3l7 4 7-4\"></path></svg></div><div class=\"min-w-0\"><div class=\"font-semibold text-gray-900 dark:text-white group-hover:text-brand-700 dark:group-hover:text-brand-400 transition-colors\">Academic Search</div><div class=\"text-xs text-gray-500 dark:text-gray-400 mt-1 leading-5 line-clamp-2\">Search peer-reviewed papers and pre-prints across arXiv, PubMed, bioRxiv, and medRxiv from one endpoint. Built for AI-driven literature review, RAG over scientific corpora, and citation extraction.</div></div></div></a><a class=\"group block rounded-lg border border-gray-200 dark:border-zinc-800 bg-white dark:bg-zinc-950 p-4 hover:border-brand-300 dark:hover:border-brand-700 transition-colors\" href=\"/extract\"><div class=\"flex items-start gap-3\"><div class=\"shrink-0 mt-0.5\"><svg class=\"w-7 h-7 text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300\" fill=\"none\" stroke=\"currentColor\" viewBox=\"0 0 24 24\"><path stroke-linecap=\"round\" stroke-linejoin=\"round\" stroke-width=\"1.5\" d=\"M9 12h6m-6 4h6m2 5H7a2 2 0 01-2-2V5a2 2 0 012-2h5.586a1 1 0 01.707.293l5.414 5.414a1 1 0 01.293.707V19a2 2 0 01-2 2z\"></path></svg></div><div class=\"min-w-0\"><div class=\"font-semibold text-gray-900 dark:text-white group-hover:text-brand-700 dark:group-hover:text-brand-400 transition-colors\">URL Content Extract</div><div class=\"text-xs text-gray-500 dark:text-gray-400 mt-1 leading-5 line-clamp-2\">Extract clean readable content from up to 25 URLs per call. Strips ads, nav, and boilerplate; returns markdown-flavoured text ready for LLM ingestion. 2 credits per URL.</div></div></div></a><a class=\"group block rounded-lg border border-gray-200 dark:border-zinc-800 bg-white dark:bg-zinc-950 p-4 hover:border-brand-300 dark:hover:border-brand-700 transition-colors\" href=\"/search-clinical\"><div class=\"flex items-start gap-3\"><div class=\"shrink-0 mt-0.5\"><svg class=\"w-7 h-7 text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300\" fill=\"none\" stroke=\"currentColor\" viewBox=\"0 0 24 24\"><path stroke-linecap=\"round\" stroke-linejoin=\"round\" stroke-width=\"1.5\" d=\"M4.318 6.318a4.5 4.5 0 016.364 0L12 7.636l1.318-1.318a4.5 4.5 0 116.364 6.364L12 20.364l-7.682-7.682a4.5 4.5 0 010-6.364z\"></path></svg></div><div class=\"min-w-0\"><div class=\"font-semibold text-gray-900 dark:text-white group-hover:text-brand-700 dark:group-hover:text-brand-400 transition-colors\">Clinical Search</div><div class=\"text-xs text-gray-500 dark:text-gray-400 mt-1 leading-5 line-clamp-2\">Search clinical trials, FDA drug labels, and ChEMBL bioactivity. Built for medical research, drug repurposing, and AI-driven clinical decision support workflows.</div></div></div></a></div></section><section class=\"mt-12 mb-4 rounded-lg border border-gray-200 dark:border-zinc-800 bg-gray-50 dark:bg-zinc-900/40 p-5\"><div class=\"flex items-start gap-4\"><img src=\"/images/sarah_choy.jpeg\" alt=\"Sarah Choy\" width=\"48\" height=\"48\" class=\"shrink-0 w-12 h-12 rounded-full object-cover\"><div class=\"min-w-0\"><div class=\"text-xs uppercase tracking-widest text-gray-500 dark:text-gray-400 mb-1\">Written by</div><div class=\"text-base font-semibold text-gray-900 dark:text-white\">Sarah Choy</div><div class=\"text-sm text-gray-600 dark:text-gray-400 mb-2\">CEO, API Pick</div><p class=\"text-sm text-gray-600 dark:text-gray-400 leading-6\">Sarah Choy is the CEO of API Pick. Search</a></li><li><a class=\"text-sm text-gray-500 dark:text-gray-400 hover:text-gray-700 dark:hover:text-gray-300\" href=\"/research-search\">Research Search</a></li><li><a class=\"text-sm did arXiv start rate-limiting so aggressively in 2024?\\\\\\\",\\\\\\\"acceptedAnswer\\\\\\\":{\\\\\\\"@type\\\\\\\":\\\\\\\"Answer\\\\\\\",\\\\\\\"text\\\\\\\":\\\\\\\"LLM-driven scrapers. arXiv staff have been explicit on their developer mailing list and on @arxiv on X about the pattern: an LLM agent fans out 50 parallel requests to fetch references for a single paper, multiply by thousands of users running similar workflows, and the whole index gets degraded. The 3-second-between-requests rule was always documented, but enforcement got strict starting in late 2024 / early 2025.\\\\\\\"}},{\\\\\\\"@type\\\\\\\":\\\\\\\"Question\\\\\\\",\\\\\\\"name\\\\\\\":\\\\\\\"Is Semantic Scholar's 1,000 req/sec really shared?\\\\\\\",\\\\\\\"acceptedAnswer\\\\\\\":{\\\\\\\"@type\\\\\\\":\\\\\\\"Answer\\\\\\\",\\\\\\\"text\\\\\\\":\\\\\\\"Yes — that's the unauthenticated pool, shared across every IP that hits the public API. In practice, unauthenticated requests start failing during peak hours regardless of your individual rate. The official advice is to apply for an API key, which moves you to a per-key bucket. Application takes weeks and is granted on the assumption of academic, not commercial, use.\\\\\\\"}},{\\\\\\\"@type\\\\\\\":\\\\\\\"Question\\\\\\\",\\\\\\\"name\\\\\\\":\\\\\\\"What about PubMed's E-utils?\\\\\\\",\\\\\\\"acceptedAnswer\\\\\\\":{\\\\\\\"@type\\\\\\\":\\\\\\\"Answer\\\\\\\",\\\\\\\"text\\\\\\\":\\\\\\\"Better than the others — 3 req/sec without a key, 10 req/sec with. Apply for an NCBI API key by email; usually granted same-day for stated research purposes. Still: 10 req/sec is fine for a single user but inadequate for a multi-user product where every user-question fans out to several PubMed calls.\\\\\\\"}},{\\\\\\\"@type\\\\\\\":\\\\\\\"Question\\\\\\\",\\\\\\\"name\\\\\\\":\\\\\\\"Why does PaperQA2 work where my homegrown agent doesn't?\\\\\\\",\\\\\\\"acceptedAnswer\\\\\\\":{\\\\\\\"@type\\\\\\\":\\\\\\\"Answer\\\\\\\",\\\\\\\"text\\\\\\\":\\\\\\\"Three reasons. (1) PaperQA2 batches and caches aggressively — the same DOI lookup is never made twice. (2) It uses Semantic Scholar primarily for its citation graph (one call per paper) rather than as a search index. (3) It accepts a longer wall-clock per question in exchange for not exceeding limits. If you want the same UX in a product where users expect 5-second responses, you need a higher-throughput layer.\\\\\\\"}},{\\\\\\\"@type\\\\\\\":\\\\\\\"Question\\\\\\\",\\\\\\\"name\\\\\\\":\\\\\\\"What does API Pick Academic Search actually solve?\\\\\\\",\\\\\\\"acceptedAnswer\\\\\\\":{\\\\\\\"@type\\\\\\\":\\\\\\\"Answer\\\\\\\",\\\\\\\"text\\\\\\\":\\\\\\\"It manages the rate limits and source coverage so your agent doesn't have to. One POST /api/search/academic call returns ranked results from arXiv, PubMed, bioRxiv, and medRxiv together, pre-shaped for LLM consumption. 5 credits per call (≈$0.005), only deducted on HTTP 200. Rate-Limited\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"$L17\\\",null,{\\\"post\\\":{\\\"slug\\\":\\\"scientific-literature-agent-without-rate-limits\\\",\\\"locale\\\":\\\"en\\\",\\\"title\\\":\\\"How to Build a Scientific Literature-Review Agent Without Getting Rate-Limited\\\",\\\"description\\\":\\\"arXiv 429s, Semantic Scholar's shared rate limit, PubMed's 3-per-second cap — the rate limits on free academic APIs are eating LLM-driven research agents. Here's how to build a working literature-review agent that actually finishes.\\\",\\\"excerpt\\\":\\\"Build a literature-review agent on raw arXiv + PubMed + Semantic Scholar today and you'll hit 429s before you finish ten papers. Here's why the rate limits got worse, what PaperQA / Undermind actually do under the hood, and a working pattern that survives a real review session.\\\",\\\"tldr\\\":[\\\"arXiv began throttling aggressively in late 2024 after LLM scrapers triggered 429 storms; the documented limit is 1 request every 3 seconds, but real-world burst tolerance is lower.\\\",\\\"Semantic Scholar's 1,000 req/sec is shared across all unauthenticated callers — effectively unusable for production agents.\\\",\\\"PubMed E-utils caps unauthenticated traffic at 3 req/sec; with an API key, 10 req/sec.\\\",\\\"Working agents (PaperQA2, Undermind, Elicit) all use a proxy / cache layer in front of these sources.\\\",\\\"API Pick Academic Search wraps arXiv, PubMed, bioRxiv, and medRxiv in one rate-managed endpoint — 5 credits per call, only-on-success.\\\"],\\\"datePublished\\\":\\\"2026-05-03\\\",\\\"dateModified\\\":\\\"2026-05-03\\\",\\\"category\\\":\\\"tutorial\\\",\\\"tags\\\":[\\\"arXiv\\\",\\\"PubMed\\\",\\\"Semantic Scholar\\\",\\\"Scientific RAG\\\",\\\"Literature Review\\\"],\\\"authorId\\\":\\\"sarah-choy\\\",\\\"readMin\\\":10,\\\"isHowTo\\\":true,\\\"relatedTools\\\":[\\\"/search-academic\\\",\\\"/extract\\\",\\\"/search-clinical\\\"],\\\"faqs\\\":[{\\\"q\\\":\\\"Why did arXiv start rate-limiting so aggressively in 2024?\\\",\\\"a\\\":\\\"LLM-driven scrapers. arXiv staff have been explicit on their developer mailing list and on @arxiv on X about the pattern: an LLM agent fans out 50 parallel requests to fetch references for a single paper, multiply by thousands of users running similar workflows, and the whole index gets degraded. The 3-second-between-requests rule was always documented, but enforcement got strict starting in late 2024 / early 2025.\\\"},{\\\"q\\\":\\\"Is Semantic Scholar's 1,000 req/sec really shared?\\\",\\\"a\\\":\\\"Yes — that's the unauthenticated pool, shared across every IP that hits the public API. In practice, unauthenticated requests start failing during peak hours regardless of your individual rate. The official advice is to apply for an API key, which moves you to a per-key bucket. Application takes weeks and is granted on the assumption of academic, not commercial, use.\\\"},{\\\"q\\\":\\\"What about PubMed's E-utils?\\\",\\\"a\\\":\\\"Better than the others — 3 req/sec without a key, 10 req/sec with. Apply for an NCBI API key by email; usually granted same-day for stated research purposes. Still: 10 req/sec is fine for a single user but inadequate for a multi-user product where every user-question fans out to several PubMed calls.\\\"},{\\\"q\\\":\\\"Why does PaperQA2 work where my homegrown agent doesn't?\\\",\\\"a\\\":\\\"Three reasons. (1) PaperQA2 batches and caches aggressively — the same DOI lookup is never made twice. (2) It uses Semantic Scholar primarily for its citation graph (one call per paper) rather than as a search index. (3) It accepts a longer wall-clock per question in exchange for not exceeding limits. If you want the same UX in a product where users expect 5-second responses, you need a higher-throughput layer.\\\"},{\\\"q\\\":\\\"What does API Pick Academic Search actually solve?\\\",\\\"a\\\":\\\"It manages the rate limits and source coverage so your agent doesn't have to. One \\u003ccode\\u003ePOST /api/search/academic\\u003c/code\\u003e call returns ranked results from arXiv, PubMed, bioRxiv, and medRxiv together, pre-shaped for LLM consumption. 5 credits per call (≈$0.005), only deducted on HTTP 200. You get to focus on the agent loop and the prompt; the throttling is our problem.\\\"}]},\\\"authorName\\\":\\\"Sarah Choy\\\"}],false,[\\\"$\\\",\\\"div\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"mt-6 mb-8 rounded-md overflow-hidden border border-zinc-200 dark:border-zinc-800 relative\\\",\\\"children\\\":[[\\\"$\\\",\\\"span\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"absolute -top-1.5 -left-1.5 h-3 w-3 border-t border-l border-zinc-400/60 dark:border-cyan-500/40 z-10\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"span\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"absolute -top-1.5 -right-1.5 h-3 w-3 border-t border-r border-zinc-400/60 dark:border-cyan-500/40 z-10\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"span\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"absolute -bottom-1.5 -left-1.5 h-3 w-3 border-b border-l border-zinc-400/60 dark:border-cyan-500/40 z-10\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"span\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"absolute -bottom-1.5 -right-1.5 h-3 w-3 border-b border-r border-zinc-400/60 dark:border-cyan-500/40 z-10\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"img\\\",null,{\\\"src\\\":\\\"/og/blog/scientific-literature-agent-without-rate-limits.webp\\\",\\\"alt\\\":\\\"How to Build a Scientific Literature-Review Agent Without Getting Rate-Limited\\\",\\\"className\\\":\\\"w-full h-auto block\\\"}]]}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"p\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"text-lg text-zinc-600 dark:text-zinc-300 leading-relaxed\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"Build a literature-review agent on raw arXiv + PubMed + Semantic Scholar today and you'll hit 429s before you finish ten papers. Now every undergraduate with Python writes an LLM agent that fans out fifty parallel calls to read one paper's references. dark:bg-brand-950/20\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"5 credits/call (~$0.005)\\\"}]]]}]]}]]}]]}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"h2\\\",null,{\\\"id\\\":\\\"what-working-products-actually-do\\\",\\\"className\\\":\\\"scroll-mt-24 text-2xl md:text-3xl font-bold tracking-tight text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-12 mb-4\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"What working products actually do\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"p\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\\\",\\\"children\\\":[\\\"PaperQA2, Undermind, Elicit, ResearchRabbit, and the agentic RAG papers (e.g. \\\",[\\\"$\\\",\\\"em\\\",null,{\\\"children\\\":\\\"Open-Source Agentic Hybrid RAG Framework\\\"}],\\\", arXiv 2508.05660) all converge on a similar pattern. Three engineering moves matter most:\\\"]}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"h3\\\",null,{\\\"id\\\":\\\"1-cache-by-doi-arxiv-id-not-by-query\\\",\\\"className\\\":\\\"scroll-mt-24 text-xl font-semibold text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-8 mb-3\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"1. Cache by DOI / arXiv ID, not by query\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"p\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\\\",\\\"children\\\":[\\\"The same paper gets requested by many different queries. Caching at the search-result level barely helps; caching at the paper-identifier level does. A small Redis (or even SQLite) layer keyed on \\\",[\\\"$\\\",\\\"code\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"font-mono text-[0.85em] bg-gray-100 dark:bg-zinc-800 text-brand-700 dark:text-brand-400 px-1.5 py-0.5 rounded\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"doi:10.1038/...\\\"}],\\\" pays itself back in one afternoon of agent traffic.\\\"]}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"h3\\\",null,{\\\"id\\\":\\\"2-treat-the-citation-graph-as-the-slow-changing-index\\\",\\\"className\\\":\\\"scroll-mt-24 text-xl font-semibold text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-8 mb-3\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"2. Treat the citation graph as the slow-changing index\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"p\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"Semantic Scholar's strength isn't keyword search; it's the citation graph. PaperQA2 uses it to expand from one seed paper to a related cluster, not to discover papers from scratch. That's a much smaller request volume — one call per paper, not hundreds — and stays well under the rate limit.\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"h3\\\",null,{\\\"id\\\":\\\"3-accept-latency-as-the-trade-off-or-proxy-the-rate-limit\\\",\\\"className\\\":\\\"scroll-mt-24 text-xl font-semibold text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-8 mb-3\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"3. Accept latency as the trade-off, OR proxy the rate limit\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"p\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"Either you make users wait 30-60 seconds for a careful, throttle-respecting query (PaperQA2's choice), or you add a layer that aggregates traffic across users and presents a single burst-tolerant interface to the agent (the API Pick choice). Both work. Mixing them — a low-latency UX over rate-limited public APIs without a buffer — is what fails.\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"h2\\\",null,{\\\"id\\\":\\\"working-code-a-literature-agent-that-finishes\\\",\\\"className\\\":\\\"scroll-mt-24 text-2xl md:text-3xl font-bold tracking-tight text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-12 mb-4\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"Working code: a literature agent that finishes\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"p\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"The minimum viable agent that survives a real review session:\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"div\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"my-5\\\",\\\"children\\\":[\\\"$\\\",\\\"$L18\\\",null,{\\\"language\\\":\\\"python\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"import requests\\\\nfrom anthropic import Anthropic\\\\n\\\\nKEY = \\\\\\\"pk_yourkey\\\\\\\"\\\\nclient = Anthropic()\\\\n\\\\ndef fetch_tool(path: str) -\\u003e dict:\\\\n    return requests.get(f\\\\\\\"https://www.apipick.com{path}/tool-schema\\\\\\\").json()[\\\\\\\"claude\\\\\\\"]\\\\n\\\\n# Two tools: academic search + URL extract for the full body\\\\nTOOLS = [\\\\n    fetch_tool(\\\\\\\"/api/search/academic\\\\\\\"),\\\\n    fetch_tool(\\\\\\\"/api/extract\\\\\\\"),\\\\n]\\\\n\\\\nSYSTEM = \\\\\\\"\\\\\\\"\\\\\\\"You are a literature-review research assistant. Process:\\\\n\\\\n1. Use academic_search with the user's question to find relevant papers\\\\n   from arXiv, PubMed, bioRxiv, and medRxiv. One call usually returns\\\\n   the right set of seed papers.\\\\n\\\\n2. For papers worth citing in detail, use extract_urls on the paper's URL\\\\n   to pull the body. Batch up to 5 URLs per call.\\\\n\\\\n3. Answer the user's question with inline citations in the form\\\\n   [Author Year, doi/arxiv URL]. Quote findings verbatim where possible.\\\\n\\\\n4. If the search returned \\u003c3 substantive results, expand the query and\\\\n   try once more. Don't loop indefinitely — say \\\\\\\"I couldn't find a strong\\\\n   answer in the indexed literature\\\\\\\" if nothing matches.\\\\n\\\\nBe precise. Cite every factual claim. Distinguish preprints (arXiv,\\\\nbioRxiv, medRxiv) from peer-reviewed (PubMed) when it matters.\\\\\\\"\\\\\\\"\\\\\\\"\\\\n\\\\ndef call_tool(block):\\\\n    name_to_path = {\\\\\\\"academic_search\\\\\\\": \\\\\\\"/api/search/academic\\\\\\\", \\\\\\\"extract_urls\\\\\\\": \\\\\\\"/api/extract\\\\\\\"}\\\\n    r = requests.post(\\\\n        f\\\\\\\"https://www.apipick.com{name_to_path[block.name]}\\\\\\\",\\\\n        json=block.input,\\\\n        headers={\\\\\\\"x-api-key\\\\\\\": KEY},\\\\n        timeout=60,\\\\n    )\\\\n    return {\\\\\\\"type\\\\\\\": \\\\\\\"tool_result\\\\\\\", \\\\\\\"tool_use_id\\\\\\\": block.id,\\\\n            \\\\\\\"content\\\\\\\": r.text, \\\\\\\"is_error\\\\\\\": r.status_code != 200}\\\\n\\\\ndef review(question: str) -\\u003e str:\\\\n    msgs = [{\\\\\\\"role\\\\\\\": \\\\\\\"user\\\\\\\", \\\\\\\"content\\\\\\\": question}]\\\\n    while True:\\\\n        r = client.messages.create(\\\\n            model=\\\\\\\"claude-sonnet-4-6\\\\\\\",\\\\n            max_tokens=4096,\\\\n            system=SYSTEM,\\\\n            tools=TOOLS,\\\\n            messages=msgs,\\\\n        )\\\\n        msgs.append({\\\\\\\"role\\\\\\\": \\\\\\\"assistant\\\\\\\", \\\\\\\"content\\\\\\\": r.content})\\\\n        if r.stop_reason == \\\\\\\"end_turn\\\\\\\":\\\\n            return \\\\\\\"\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\".join(b.text for b in r.content if b.type == \\\\\\\"text\\\\\\\")\\\\n        if r.stop_reason == \\\\\\\"tool_use\\\\\\\":\\\\n            results = [call_tool(b) for b in r.content if b.type == \\\\\\\"tool_use\\\\\\\"]\\\\n            msgs.append({\\\\\\\"role\\\\\\\": \\\\\\\"user\\\\\\\", \\\\\\\"content\\\\\\\": results})\\\\n\\\\nprint(review(\\\\\\\"Recent advances in LLM-based protein structure prediction (2025)\\\\\\\"))\\\"}]}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"p\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"Cost per question:\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"ul\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"list-disc ms-6 space-y-2 text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\\\",\\\"children\\\":[[\\\"$\\\",\\\"li\\\",null,{\\\"children\\\":\\\"1-2 academic_search calls (5-10 credits = $0.005-$0.010)\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"li\\\",null,{\\\"children\\\":\\\"1 extract call covering 3-5 papers (6-10 credits = $0.006-$0.010)\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"li\\\",null,{\\\"children\\\":\\\"~5,000 input + 1,200 output tokens to Claude (~$0.04)\\\"}]]}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"p\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"Round figure: ~5 cents per literature-review answer with citations. At 100 questions/day that's $5/day — about what one reasonable researcher's daily caffeine costs.\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"aside\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"my-6 rounded-lg border px-4 py-3 text-sm leading-6 bg-violet-50 dark:bg-violet-950/40 border-violet-200 dark:border-violet-900 text-violet-900 dark:text-violet-100\\\",\\\"children\\\":[[\\\"$\\\",\\\"div\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"font-semibold mb-1\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"When NOT to use this pattern\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"div\\\",null,{\\\"children\\\":\\\"Bulk literature mining (downloading millions of papers for training data) is a different problem. Use OpenAlex bulk dumps for that — they're explicitly designed for it and free. The pattern in this article is for interactive, per-question agent calls where users wait for answers in seconds, not hours.\\\"}]]}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"h2\\\",null,{\\\"id\\\":\\\"sub-vertical-tweaks\\\",\\\"className\\\":\\\"scroll-mt-24 text-2xl md:text-3xl font-bold tracking-tight text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-12 mb-4\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"Sub-vertical tweaks\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"h3\\\",null,{\\\"id\\\":\\\"biomedical-literature\\\",\\\"className\\\":\\\"scroll-mt-24 text-xl font-semibold text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-8 mb-3\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"Biomedical literature\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"p\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\\\",\\\"children\\\":[\\\"Bias the agent toward PubMed (peer-reviewed) and explicitly mark bioRxiv/medRxiv hits as preprints. When asking \\\",[\\\"$\\\",\\\"em\\\",null,{\\\"children\\\":\\\"\\\\\\\"what does the latest evidence say\\\\\\\"\\\"}],\\\", the agent should weight peer-reviewed higher. A line in the system prompt — \\\",[\\\"$\\\",\\\"em\\\",null,{\\\"children\\\":\\\"\\\\\\\"If preprint and peer-reviewed sources disagree, defer to peer-reviewed and note the discrepancy\\\\\\\"\\\"}],\\\" — handles this cleanly.\\\"]}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"h3\\\",null,{\\\"id\\\":\\\"mathematical-cs\\\",\\\"className\\\":\\\"scroll-mt-24 text-xl font-semibold text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-8 mb-3\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"Mathematical / CS\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"p\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"arXiv dominates here. The signal-to-noise ratio is better than in biomed, and citations matter more than recency for foundational work. Search with broader queries and let the agent prune.\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"h3\\\",null,{\\\"id\\\":\\\"drug-discovery-clinical\\\",\\\"className\\\":\\\"scroll-mt-24 text-xl font-semibold text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-8 mb-3\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"Drug discovery / clinical\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"p\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\\\",\\\"children\\\":[\\\"Pair with \\\",[\\\"$\\\",\\\"$L19\\\",null,{\\\"href\\\":\\\"/search-clinical\\\",\\\"className\\\":\\\"text-brand-700 dark:text-brand-400 hover:underline underline-offset-2\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"Clinical Search\\\"}],\\\" (ClinicalTrials.gov + FDA labels + ChEMBL + DrugBank) for the regulatory and bioactivity dimensions that academic search can't cover. The combination — peer-reviewed literature + trial registry + structural data — is how a drug-repurposing or pharmacovigilance agent gets useful.\\\"]}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"h2\\\",null,{\\\"id\\\":\\\"where-this-generalises\\\",\\\"className\\\":\\\"scroll-mt-24 text-2xl md:text-3xl font-bold tracking-tight text-gray-900 dark:text-white mt-12 mb-4\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"Where this generalises\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"p\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"The rate-limit problem is not unique to academic search. Any open public dataset that shipped APIs in the pre-LLM era is being subjected to the same load patterns now: SEC EDGAR, USPTO, EPO, public-records databases, weather services, government open data. The same engineering pattern works for all of them — cache at the entity level, layer a managed proxy, accept latency as the alternative when you can't afford the proxy.\\\"}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"p\\\",null,{\\\"className\\\":\\\"text-gray-700 dark:text-gray-300 leading-7\\\",\\\"children\\\":[\\\"The deeper shift: in 2026 it's no longer reasonable to expect a free public API to absorb LLM-agent load directly. The endpoints aren't disappearing — but they're getting wrapped by a layer of paid managed services that exists to translate \\\\\\\"polite human researcher\\\\\\\" rate limits into \\\\\\\"burst-tolerant agent traffic\\\\\\\". \\\",[\\\"$\\\",\\\"$L19\\\",null,{\\\"href\\\":\\\"/search-academic\\\",\\\"className\\\":\\\"text-brand-700 dark:text-brand-400 hover:underline underline-offset-2\\\",\\\"children\\\":\\\"API Pick Academic Search\\\"}],\\\" is one of those layers for the literature-review use case. Expect more.\\\"]}]],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"$L1a\\\",null,{\\\"faqs\\\":[{\\\"q\\\":\\\"Why did arXiv start rate-limiting so aggressively in 2024?\\\",\\\"a\\\":\\\"LLM-driven scrapers. arXiv staff have been explicit on their developer mailing list and on @arxiv on X about the pattern: an LLM agent fans out 50 parallel requests to fetch references for a single paper, multiply by thousands of users running similar workflows, and the whole index gets degraded. The 3-second-between-requests rule was always documented, but enforcement got strict starting in late 2024 / early 2025.\\\"},{\\\"q\\\":\\\"Is Semantic Scholar's 1,000 req/sec really shared?\\\",\\\"a\\\":\\\"Yes — that's the unauthenticated pool, shared across every IP that hits the public API. In practice, unauthenticated requests start failing during peak hours regardless of your individual rate. The official advice is to apply for an API key, which moves you to a per-key bucket. Application takes weeks and is granted on the assumption of academic, not commercial, use.\\\"},{\\\"q\\\":\\\"What about PubMed's E-utils?\\\",\\\"a\\\":\\\"Better than the others — 3 req/sec without a key, 10 req/sec with. Apply for an NCBI API key by email; usually granted same-day for stated research purposes. Still: 10 req/sec is fine for a single user but inadequate for a multi-user product where every user-question fans out to several PubMed calls.\\\"},{\\\"q\\\":\\\"Why does PaperQA2 work where my homegrown agent doesn't?\\\",\\\"a\\\":\\\"Three reasons. (1) PaperQA2 batches and caches aggressively — the same DOI lookup is never made twice. (2) It uses Semantic Scholar primarily for its citation graph (one call per paper) rather than as a search index. (3) It accepts a longer wall-clock per question in exchange for not exceeding limits. If you want the same UX in a product where users expect 5-second responses, you need a higher-throughput layer.\\\"},{\\\"q\\\":\\\"What does API Pick Academic Search actually solve?\\\",\\\"a\\\":\\\"It manages the rate limits and source coverage so your agent doesn't have to. One \\u003ccode\\u003ePOST /api/search/academic\\u003c/code\\u003e call returns ranked results from arXiv, PubMed, bioRxiv, and medRxiv together, pre-shaped for LLM consumption. 5 credits per call (≈$0.005), only deducted on HTTP 200. You get to focus on the agent loop and the prompt; the throttling is our problem.\\\"}]}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"$L1b\\\",null,{\\\"hrefs\\\":[\\\"/search-academic\\\",\\\"/extract\\\",\\\"/search-clinical\\\"]}],[\\\"$\\\",\\\"$L1c\\\",null,{\\\"author\\\":{\\\"id\\\":\\\"sarah-choy\\\",\\\"name\\\":\\\"Sarah Choy\\\",\\\"role\\\":\\\"CEO, API Pick\\\",\\\"bioKey\\\":\\\"sarahChoy\\\",\\\"url\\\":\\\"https://www.apipick.com/about\\\",\\\"sameAs\\\":[],\\\"image\\\":\\\"/images/sarah_choy.jpeg\\\"}}]]}]\\n\"])</script><next-route-announcer style=\"position: absolute;\"></next-route-announcer></body></html>",
